##-----------------TITLE------------------------##
Ray-Intersection Diagram
##------------------TEXT------------------------##
Closest Pair Applications: Ray-Intersection Diagram
(or, Crashing Motorcycles Efficiently)

Click and drag to specify the initial locations and velocities of a
system of moving particles.  Each particle stops moving when it crosses
the track left by another particle.







If you were viewing this on a Java-enabled browser, you'd get to play
with my extremely exciting applet.  Since you're not, you might as well
just follow the following links, since I have no other content here:



For more detailed information on this diagram,
see Jeff Erickson's page
"crashing
motorcycles efficiently".  This implementation is based on the
FastPair version of our closest pair data
structures (with nearest neighbors found by sequential search rather than
geometric range searching); see the source code
for details.


David Eppstein,
Dept. Information & Computer Science,
UC Irvine,
.

Prev: Avila Pier, IVUp: Avila Beach and EnvironsNext: Port San Luis Pier Pelican, II
Port San Luis Pier Pelican, I

This brown pelican was sitting at the end of the Port San Luis Pier.  As I crouched down some distance away to take its photo, it flew over to within arms reach of me, obviously hoping for a handout and perhaps thinking my pair of sunglasses was a fish.  Disappointed, it soon flew away.

##-----------------TITLE------------------------##
Banff From Sulphur Mountain
##------------------TEXT------------------------##
Prev: Sulphur Mountain Gondola Station, IIUp: BanffNext: Sanson Station Graffiti, I
Banff From Sulphur Mountain

The low hill in the middle is Tunnel Mountain, so called because they didn't build a railroad tunnel through it, and the complex at the base of the mountain is Banff Centre, where WADS was held. The hour and a half between the talks and the banquet on Saturday evening was (barely) enough to hike to the top of it and back. The town is to the left of the hill, and the Banff Lodge is on this side of the Bow River from the hill. The hoodoos on the river are where it meets a low bluff in the right background.

##-----------------TITLE------------------------##
Me Climbing
##------------------TEXT------------------------##
Prev: Rocktop FigureUp: Semiannual playgroup campout in Joshua Tree, April 2002Next: Me Topping Out
Me Climbing

Photo taken by Diana.  The big underhang at my right hand makes this part easy — the only tricky move
was earlier, when I had my right foot in the lower right corner, right hand on the outcrop near where
my left foot is in the picture, and left hand on the flat rock to the left, in order to get enough leverage
to pull my other foot up from an overhang below the photo.  You can judge my level of seriousness by the clothes...
